## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |

| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

**Sourcegraph Repository:** `github.com/sg-evals/ceph--v19.2.1`

# Task: Security Audit of Ceph RADOS Gateway S3 Authentication

## Objective
Perform a security audit of the S3 authentication implementation in Ceph's RADOS Gateway (RGW) and create a findings report with remediation recommendations.

## Steps
1. Find the S3 authentication implementation in `src/rgw/` (look for AWS Signature V4 handling)
2. Identify the request signing and verification flow
3. Check for common S3 auth vulnerabilities:
   - Signature version fallback (V2 vs V4)
   - Timing attacks in signature comparison
   - Request replay prevention (timestamp validation window)
   - Secret key storage and access patterns
4. Create `security_audit.md` in `/workspace/` documenting:
   - Authentication flow overview (file paths and key functions)
   - Each finding with severity, description, file location, and remediation
   - At least 3 specific findings with code references
   - Summary risk assessment

## Key Reference Files
- `src/rgw/rgw_auth_s3.h` and `src/rgw/rgw_auth_s3.cc` — S3 auth
- `src/rgw/rgw_rest_s3.cc` — S3 REST handler
- `src/rgw/rgw_auth.h` — auth framework

## Success Criteria
- security_audit.md exists
- Contains file paths from src/rgw/
- Identifies at least 3 security findings
- Includes remediation recommendations

342026-03-11T03:16:53.168987agentmessage-
I am thinking...: Now I have a comprehensive understanding of the S3 authentication implementation. Let me analyze the key security findings:

1. **Timing Attack in Signature Comparison** (HIGH severity):
   - In `LocalEngine::authenticate()` (rgw_rest_s3.cc:6317-6329) and `STSEngine::authenticate()` (rgw_rest_s3.cc:6451-6464), the signature comparison uses `signature.compare(server_signature)` which is `std::string::compare()` - a non-constant-time comparison. This is vulnerable to timing attacks.
   - Same issue in `AWSv4ComplSingle::complete()` (rgw_auth_s3.cc:1714): `payload_hash.compare(expected_request_payload_hash) == 0`
   - Same issue in `AWSv4ComplMulti::is_signature_mismatched()` (rgw_auth_s3.cc:1228, 1231): `chunk_meta.get_signature() == prev_chunk_signature` and `chunk_meta.get_signature() == calc_signature` - these use `std::string::operator==` which is also not constant-time.
   - The fix would be to use a constant-time comparison function like `CRYPTO_memcmp()` from OpenSSL.

2. **Signature Version Fallback (V2 vs V4)** (MEDIUM severity):
   - The `AWSGeneralAbstractor::get_auth_data()` method (in rgw_rest_s3.cc) supports both V2 and V4 signatures. The system accepts both AWS Signature V2 (HMAC-SHA1) and V4 (HMAC-SHA256). V2 is significantly weaker.
   - Looking at the code, `get_auth_data_v2()` uses `get_v2_signature` which uses HMAC-SHA1 (weaker than SHA256).
   - The `AWSAuthStrategy` template allows both V2 and V4 through the `AWSGeneralAbstractor`.
   - There's no configuration option visible to disable V2 entirely.

3. **Timestamp Validation Window** (MEDIUM severity):
   - The `RGW_AUTH_GRACE` is set to 15 minutes (rgw_auth_s3.h:30): `static constexpr auto RGW_AUTH_GRACE = std::chrono::minutes{15};`
   - This is a fixed 15-minute window that canno
... (truncated)

Derivative is supposed to encapsulate engine\\\\n331:  * instances and add them using the add_engine() method in the order it\\\\n332:  * wants to be tried during the call to authenticate().\\\\n333:  *\\\\n334:  * Each new Strategy should be exposed to StrategyRegistry for handling\\\\n335:  * the dynamic reconfiguration. */\\\\n336: class Strategy : public Engine {\\\\n337: public:\\\\n338:   /* Specifiers controlling what happens when an associated engine fails.\\\\n339:    * The names and semantic has been borrowed mostly from libpam. */\\\\n340:   enum class Control {\\\\n341:     /* Failure of an engine injected with the REQUISITE specifier aborts\\\\n342:      * the strategy's authentication process immediately. No other engine\\\\n343:      * will be tried. */\\\\n344:     REQUISITE,\\\\n345: \\\\n346:     /* Success of an engine injected with the SUFFICIENT specifier ends\\\\n347:      * strategy's authentication process successfully. However, denying\\\\n348:      * doesn't abort it -- there will be fall-back to following engine\\\\n349:      * if the one that failed wasn't the last one. */\\\\n350:     SUFFICIENT,\\\\n351: \\\\n352:     /* Like SUFFICIENT with the exception that on failure the reason code\\\\n353:      * is not overridden. Typical examples are AWS Auth v4 and the auth mechanism\\n158:  * of browser uploads facilities both in S3 and Swift APIs (see RGWPostObj).\\n159:  * The workflow of request from the authentication point-of-view does look\\n160:  * like following one:\\n161:  *  A. authenticate (Engine::authenticate),\\n162:  *  B. authorize (see RGWOp::verify_permissions),\\n163:  *  C. execute-prepare (init potential data modifications),\\n164:  *  D. authenticate-complete - (Completer::complete),\\n165:  *  E. execute-commit - commit the modifications from point C. */\\n166: class Completer {\\n167: public:\\n168:   /* It's expected that Completers would tend to implement many interfaces\\n169:    * and be used not only in req_state::auth::completer. Ref counting their\\n170:    * instances would be helpful. */\\n171:   typedef std::shared_ptr<Completer> cmplptr_t;\\n172: \\n173:   virtual ~Completer() = default;\\n174: \\n175:   /* Complete the authentication process. Typical use case is verifying message integrity\\n196:  *    in AWS Auth v4 and browser uploads (RGWPostObj).\\n197:  *\\n198:  * Both of them are supposed to be wrapped in Engine::AuthResult.\\n199:  *\\n200:  * The authentication process consists of two steps:\\n201:  *  - Engine::authenticate() which should be called before *initiating*\\n202:  *    any modifications to RADOS store that are related to an operation\\n203:  *    a client wants to perform (RGWOp::execute).\\n204:  *  - Completer::complete() supposed to be called, if completer has been\\n205:  *    returned, after the authenticate() step but before *committing*\\n206:  *    those modifications or sending a response (RGWOp::complete).\\n207:  *\\n208:  * An engine outlives both Applier and Completer.   "thought": "Now I have a comprehensive understanding of the S3 authentication implementation. Let me analyze the key security findings:\n\n1. **Timing Attack in Signature Comparison** (HIGH severity):\n   - In `LocalEngine::authenticate()` (rgw_rest_s3.cc:6317-6329) and `STSEngine::authenticate()` (rgw_rest_s3.cc:6451-6464), the signature comparison uses `signature.compare(server_signature)` which is `std::string::compare()` - a non-constant-time comparison. This is vulnerable to timing attacks.\n   - Same issue in `AWSv4ComplSingle::complete()` (rgw_auth_s3.cc:1714): `payload_hash.compare(expected_request_payload_hash) == 0`\n   - Same issue in `AWSv4ComplMulti::is_signature_mismatched()` (rgw_auth_s3.cc:1228, 1231): `chunk_meta.get_signature() == prev_chunk_signature` and `chunk_meta.get_signature() == calc_signature` - these use `std::string::operator==` which is also not constant-time.\n   - The fix would be to use a constant-time comparison function like `CRYPTO_memcmp()` from OpenSSL.\n\n2. **Signature Version Fallback (V2 vs V4)** (MEDIUM severity):\n   - The `AWSGeneralAbstractor::get_auth_data()` method (in rgw_rest_s3.cc) supports both V2 and V4 signatures. The system accepts both AWS Signature V2 (HMAC-SHA1) and V4 (HMAC-SHA256). V2 is significantly weaker.\n   - Looking at the code, `get_auth_data_v2()` uses `get_v2_signature` which uses HMAC-SHA1 (weaker than SHA256).\n   - The `AWSAuthStrategy` template allows both V2 and V4 through the `AWSGeneralAbstractor`.\n   - There's no configuration option visible to disable V2 entirely.\n\n3. **Timestamp Validation Window** (MEDIUM severity):\n   - The `RGW_AUTH_GRACE` is set to 15 minutes (rgw_auth_s3.h:30): `static constexpr auto RGW_AUTH_GRACE = std::chrono::minutes{15};`\n   - This is a fixed 15-minute window that cannot be configured. AWS recommends 5 minutes.\n   - For V4 header auth, `is_time_skew_ok()` is called (rgw_auth_s3.cc:457).\n   - For V2 query string auth (presigned URLs), the `Expires` parameter is checked but there's no upper bound on how far in the future it can be set (rgw_rest_s3.cc:6011-6016).\n   - For V4 presigned URLs, the max expiry is 7 days (604800 seconds) which is enforced (rgw_auth_s3.cc:309).\n   - For V2 header auth, `is_time_skew_ok(header_time)` is called (rgw_rest_s3.cc:6056).\n\n4. **Secret Key Logging** (MEDIUM severity):\n   - In `get_v4_signing_key()` (rgw_auth_s3.cc:996-999), intermediate signing keys are logged at debug level 10:\n     ```\n     ldpp_dout(dpp, 10) << \"date_k    = \" << date_k << dendl;\n     ldpp_dout(dpp, 10) << \"region_k  = \" << region_k << dendl;\n     ldpp_dout(dpp, 10) << \"service_k = \" << service_k << dendl;\n     ldpp_dout(dpp, 10) << \"signing_k = \" << signing_key << dendl;\n     ```\n   - These intermediate keys are derived from the secret key and could be used to forge signatures if logs are compromised.\n   - The generated signature is also logged: `ldpp_dout(dpp, 10) << \"generated signature = \" << signature << dendl;` (rgw_auth_s3.cc:1032)\n\n5. **No Replay Prevention** (MEDIUM severity):\n   - There's no nonce or request ID tracking to prevent replay attacks within the 15-minute window.\n   - An attacker who captures a valid signed request can replay it within the 15-minute window.\n   - AWS itself doesn't prevent replays within the timestamp window, but some implementations add nonce tracking.\n\n6. **V2 Presigned URL Expiry Not Bounded** (LOW-MEDIUM severity):\n   - For V2 query string auth (rgw_rest_s3.cc:6011-6016), the `Expires` parameter is just checked against `now`. There's no maximum expiry time enforced (unlike V4 which has a 7-day max).\n   - This means V2 presigned URLs can be created with arbitrarily long expiry times.\n\n7. **Chunk Signature Comparison** (MEDIUM severity):\n   - In `AWSv4ComplMulti::is_signature_mismatched()` (rgw_auth_s3.cc:1225-1232), chunk signatures are compared using `==` operator on `std::string`, which is not constant-time.\n\nLet me now look at the `get_auth_data` method to understand the V2/V4 selection logic.\n"

| Defines the 15-minute replay window |\n| `src/rgw/rgw_auth_s3.cc:265` | `is_time_skew_ok()` | Validates request timestamp against server clock |\n| `src/rgw/rgw_auth_s3.cc:978` | `get_v4_signing_key()` | Derives HMAC-SHA256 signing key from secret |\n| `src/rgw/rgw_auth_s3.cc:1013` | `get_v4_signature()` | Computes server-side AWS SigV4 signature |\n| `src/rgw/rgw_auth_s3.cc:1037` | `get_v2_signature()` | Computes server-side AWS SigV2 signature (HMAC-SHA1) |\n| `src/rgw/rgw_auth_s3.cc:1199` | `is_signature_mismatched()` | Chunk-level signature verification for streaming uploads |\n| `src/rgw/rgw_auth_s3.cc:1706` | `AWSv4ComplSingle::complete()` | Payload hash verification for single-chunk uploads |\n| `src/rgw/rgw_rest_s3.cc:5555` | `AWSGeneralAbstractor::get_auth_data()` | Dispatches to V2 or V4 auth path |\n| `src/rgw/rgw_rest_s3.cc:6265` | `LocalEngine::authenticate()` | Final signature comparison against stored secret key |\n| `src/rgw/rgw_rest_s3.cc:6407` | `STSEngine::authenticate()` | STS token-based signature comparison |\n\n### Signature Verification Flow (V4)\n\n1. **Parse credentials** \u2014 `parse_v4_credentials()` extracts `access_key_id`, `credential_scope`, `signed_headers`, `signature`, `date`, `session_token` from the `Authorization` header or query string.\n2. **Timestamp check** \u2014 `is_time_skew_ok()` rejects requests outside the \u00b115-minute window.\n3. **Canonical request** \u2014 `get_v4_canon_req_hash()` builds the canonical request string (method + URI + query string + headers + payload hash) and SHA-256 hashes it.\n4. **String to sign** \u2014 `get_v4_string_to_sign()` assembles `\"AWS4-HMAC-SHA256\\n<date>\\n<scope>\\n<canonical_req_hash>\"`.\n5. **Signing key derivation** \u2014 `get_v4_signing_key()` computes `HMAC-SHA256(HMAC-SHA256(HMAC-SHA256(HMAC-SHA256(\"AWS4\"+secret, date), region), service), \"aws4_request\")`.\n6. **Server signature** \u2014 `get_v4_signature()` computes `HMAC-SHA256(signing_key, string_to_sign)` and hex-encodes it.\n7. **Comparison** \u2014 `LocalEngine::authenticate()` calls `signature.compare(server_signature)` to compare client and server signatures.\n8. **Payload verification** (optional) \u2014 `AWSv4ComplSingle::complete()` or `AWSv4ComplMulti::complete()` verifies the payload hash after the body is received.\n\n---\n\n## 2. Security Findings\n\n---\n\n### Finding 1: Non-Constant-Time Signature Comparison (Timing Attack)\n\n**Severity:** HIGH  \n**CWE:** CWE-208 \u2014 Observable Timing Discrepancy\n\n#### Description\n\nThe signature comparison in both `LocalEngine::authenticate()` and `STSEngine::authenticate()` uses `std::string_view::compare()` and `std::string::operator==`, which are **not constant-time** operations. These functions short-circuit on the first differing byte, leaking timing information that an attacker can exploit to recover the valid signature one byte at a time.\n\n#### Affected Locations\n\n**`src/rgw/rgw_rest_s3.cc`, lines 6317\u20136329** (`LocalEngine::authenticate`):\n```cpp\nconst VersionAbstractor::server_signature_t server_signature =\n    signature_factory(cct, k.key, string_to_sign);\nauto compare = signature.compare(server_signature);   // \u2190 NOT constant-time\n\n// ...\nif (compare != 0) {\n    return result_t::reject(-ERR_SIGNATURE_NO_MATCH);\n}\n```\n\n**`src/rgw/rgw_rest_s3.cc`, lines 6451\u20136464** (`STSEngine::authenticate`):\n```cpp\nconst VersionAbstractor::server_signature_t server_signature =\n    signature_factory(cct, token.secret_access_key, string_to_sign);\nauto compare = signature.compare(server_signature);   // \u2190 NOT constant-time\n\nif (compare != 0) {\n    return result_t::reject(-ERR_SIGNATURE_NO_MATCH);\n}\n```\n\n**`src/rgw/rgw_auth_s3.cc`, lines 1225\u20131232** (`AWSv4ComplMulti::is_signature_mismatched`):\n```cpp\nauto match_signatures = [&]() -> bool {\n    if (chunk_meta.get_offset() == 0) [[unlikely]] {\n        return chunk_meta.get_signature() == prev_chunk_signature;  // \u2190 NOT constant-time\n    }\n    return chunk_meta.get_signature() == calc_signature;            // \u2190 NOT constant-time\n};\n```\n\n**`src/rgw/rgw_auth_s3.cc`, line 1714** (`AWSv4ComplSingle::complete`):\n```cpp\nif (payload_hash.compare(expected_request_payload_hash) == 0) {    // \u2190 NOT constant-time\n    return true;\n}\n```\n\n#### Impact\n\nA remote attacker with the ability to send many crafted requests and measure response times can perform a timing side-channel attack to recover the expected HMAC signature byte-by-byte. While HMAC signatures are 64 hex characters (256 bits of entropy), timing attacks against hex string comparisons have been demonstrated in practice against similar systems. This is especially dangerous for high-value administrative credentials.\n\n#### Remediation\n\nReplace all signature comparisons with a constant-time comparison function. OpenSSL's `CRYPTO_memcmp()` (already available in the Ceph dependency tree) is the standard remedy:\n\n```cpp\n#include <openssl/crypto.h>\n\n// Replace:\nauto compare = signature.compare(server_signature);\nif (compare != 0) { ... }\n\n// With:\nbool match = (signature.size() == server_signature.size()) &&\n             (CRYPTO_memcmp(signature.data(),\n                            server_signature.data(),\n                            signature.size()) == 0);\nif (!match) { ... }\n```\n\nApply this pattern consistently in `LocalEngine::authenticate()`, `STSEngine::authenticate()`, `AWSv4ComplMulti::is_signature_mismatched()`, and `AWSv4ComplSingle::complete()`.\n\n---\n\n### Finding 2: AWS Signature Version 2 (HMAC-SHA1) Still Accepted \u2014 No Disable Mechanism\n\n**Severity:** HIGH  \n**CWE:** CWE-327 \u2014 Use of a Broken or Risky Cryptographic Algorithm\n\n#### Description\n\nThe gateway unconditionally accepts both AWS Signature Version 2 (SigV2, using HMAC-SHA1) and Version 4 (SigV4, using HMAC-SHA256). SigV2 was deprecated by AWS in 2019 and is considered cryptographically weak. HMAC-SHA1 provides only 160 bits of output, and SHA-1 has known collision vulnerabilities. There is **no configuration option to disable SigV2 acceptance**, meaning operators cannot enforce the use of the stronger SigV4 even if they want to.\n\n#### Affected Locations\n\n**`src/rgw/rgw_rest_s3.cc`, lines 5555\u20135576** (`AWSGeneralAbstractor::get_auth_data`):\n```cpp\nAWSEngine::VersionAbstractor::auth_data_t\nAWSGeneralAbstractor::get_auth_data(const req_state* const s) const\n{\n    AwsVersion version;\n    AwsRoute route;\n    std::tie(version, route) = discover_aws_flavour(s->info);\n\n    // No check here to reject V2 \u2014 both versions are always accepted\n    if (version == AwsVersion::V2) {\n        return get_auth_data_v2(s);          // \u2190 HMAC-SHA1 path\n    } else if (version == AwsVersion::V4) {\n        return get_auth_data_v4(s, route == AwsRoute::QUERY_STRING);\n    } else {\n        throw -EINVAL;\n    }\n}\n```\n\n**`src/rgw/rgw_rest_s3.cc`, lines 5988\u20136068** (`AWSGeneralAbstractor::get_auth_data_v2`):\n```cpp\n// V2 uses HMAC-SHA1 via get_v2_signature:\nreturn {\n    std::move(access_key_id),\n    std::move(signature),\n    std::move(session_token),\n    std::move(string_to_sign),\n    rgw::auth::s3::get_v2_signature,   // \u2190 HMAC-SHA1\n    null_completer_factory\n};\n```\n\n**`src/rgw/rgw_auth_s3.cc`, lines 1037\u20131062** (`get_v2_signature`):\n```cpp\nAWSEngine::VersionAbstractor::server_signature_t\nget_v2_signature(CephContext* const cct,\n                 const std::string& secret_key,\n                 const AWSEngine::VersionAbstractor::string_to_sign_t& string_to_sign)\n{\n    // ...\n    const auto digest = calc_hmac_sha1(secret_key, string_to_sign);  // \u2190 SHA-1\n    // ...\n}\n```\n\nAdditionally, SigV2 does not sign the request payload, meaning the body of any V2-authenticated request can be tampered with in transit without detection.\n\n#### Impact\n\n- Clients using SigV2 are protected only by HMAC-SHA1, which is weaker than HMAC-SHA256.\n- SigV2 does not include payload signing, allowing man-in-the-middle modification of request bodies.\n- Operators cannot enforce a V4-only policy, leaving the attack surface permanently open.\n\n#### Remediation\n\n1. **Add a configuration option** (e.g., `rgw_s3_auth_disable_v2`) to reject SigV2 requests:\n   ```cpp\n   if (version == AwsVersion::V2) {\n       if (cct->_conf->rgw_s3_auth_disable_v2) {\n           ldpp_dout(s, 5) << \"SigV2 rejected by policy\" << dendl;\n           throw -ERR_SIGNATURE_NO_MATCH;\n       }\n       return get_auth_data_v2(s);\n   }\n   ```\n2. **Default the option to `true`** in new deployments and document the migration path.\n3. **Log a deprecation warning** whenever a SigV2 request is accepted, to help operators identify clients that need upgrading.\n\n---\n\n### Finding 3: Overly Wide Timestamp Validation Window Enables Request Replay\n\n**Severity:** MEDIUM  \n**CWE:** CWE-294 \u2014 Authentication Bypass by Capture-replay\n\n#### Description\n\nThe replay-prevention window (`RGW_AUTH_GRACE`) is hardcoded to **15 minutes** and is not configurable. AWS's own documentation recommends a 5-minute window. A 15-minute window gives an attacker who captures a valid signed request (e.g., via network sniffing, log exfiltration, or a compromised proxy) a 15-minute window to replay it. Furthermore, there is **no nonce or request-ID tracking** to prevent replay of the same request multiple times within the window.\n\n#### Affected Locations\n\n**`src/rgw/rgw_auth_s3.h`, line 30** \u2014 hardcoded grace period:\n```cpp\nstatic constexpr auto RGW_AUTH_GRACE = std::chrono::minutes{15};\n```\n\n**`src/rgw/rgw_auth_s3.cc`, lines 265\u2013278** \u2014 timestamp check implementation:\n```cpp\nbool is_time_skew_ok(time_t t)\n{\n    auto req_tp = ceph::coarse_real_clock::from_time_t(t);\n    auto cur_tp = ceph::coarse_real_clock::now();\n\n    if (std::chrono::abs(cur_tp - req_tp) > RGW_AUTH_GRACE) {\n        dout(10) << \"NOTICE: request time skew too big.\" << dendl;\n        // ...\n        return false;\n    }\n    return true;\n}\n```\n\n**`src/rgw/rgw_auth_s3.cc`, lines 457\u2013459** \u2014 V4 header auth timestamp check:\n```cpp\nif (!is_time_skew_ok(internal_timegm(&t))) {\n    return -ERR_REQUEST_TIME_SKEWED;\n}\n```\n\n**`src/rgw/rgw_rest_s3.cc`, lines 6056\u20136058** \u2014 V2 header auth timestamp check:\n```cpp\nif (!qsr && !is_time_skew_ok(header_time)) {\n    throw -ERR_REQUEST_TIME_SKEWED;\n}\n```\n\nNote: For V2 **query-string** (presigned URL) auth, the `Expires` parameter is checked but there is **no maximum expiry time enforced** (unlike V4 presigned URLs which cap at 7 days). A V2 presigned URL can be created with an expiry decades in the future:\n\n**`src/rgw/rgw_rest_s3.cc`, lines 6011\u20136016**:\n```cpp\nconst time_t exp = atoll(expires.data());\ntime_t now;\ntime(&now);\n\nif (now >= exp) {\n    throw -EPERM;\n}\n// No upper bound check on exp\n```\n\n#### Impact\n\n- Any captured signed request (via network interception, log files, or browser history) can be replayed for up to 15 minutes.\n- V2 presigned URLs can be created with arbitrarily long validity periods, creating permanent access tokens that cannot be revoked without rotating the secret key.\n- Without nonce tracking, the same request can be replayed multiple times within the window (e.g., to trigger repeated object deletions or uploads).\n\n#### Remediation\n\n1. **Make the grace period configurable** and reduce the default to 5 minutes:\n   ```cpp\n   // Replace the hardcoded constant with a config lookup:\n   auto grace = std::chrono::seconds(cct->_conf->rgw_auth_grace_seconds);\n   if (std::chrono::abs(cur_tp - req_tp) > grace) { ... }\n   ```\n   Add `rgw_auth_grace_seconds` to `src/common/options/rgw.yaml.in` with a default of `300` (5 minutes).\n\n2. **Enforce a maximum expiry for V2 presigned URLs** (matching the V4 limit of 7 days):\n   ```cpp\n   const time_t exp = atoll(expires.data());\n   time_t now;\n   time(&now);\n   constexpr time_t MAX_PRESIGNED_EXPIRY = 7 * 24 * 60 * 60; // 7 days\n   if (exp - now > MAX_PRESIGNED_EXPIRY) {\n       throw -EPERM;\n   }\n   if (now >= exp) {\n       throw -EPERM;\n   }\n   ```\n\n3. **Consider implementing a short-lived nonce cache** (e.g., a bounded LRU set of recently seen `(access_key, date, signature)` tuples) to prevent replay of the same request within the window.\n\n---\n\n### Finding 4: Intermediate Signing Keys Logged at Debug Level\n\n**Severity:** MEDIUM  \n**CWE:** CWE-532 \u2014 Insertion of Sensitive Information into Log File\n\n#### Description\n\nThe `get_v4_signing_key()` function logs all four intermediate HMAC-SHA256 signing keys (`date_k`, `region_k`, `service_k`, `signing_k`) at debug log level 10. The final computed signature is also logged. These intermediate keys are cryptographically equivalent to the secret access key for the specific date/region/service scope \u2014 possession of `signing_k` allows an attacker to forge arbitrary signatures for that scope without knowing the original secret key.\n\n#### Affected Locations\n\n**`src/rgw/rgw_auth_s3.cc`, lines 996\u2013999** (`get_v4_signing_key`):\n```cpp\nldpp_dout(dpp, 10) << \"date_k    = \" << date_k << dendl;\nldpp_dout(dpp, 10) << \"region_k  = \" << region_k << dendl;\nldpp_dout(dpp, 10) << \"service_k = \" << service_k << dendl;\nldpp_dout(dpp, 10) << \"signing_k = \" << signing_key << dendl;\n```\n\n**`src/rgw/rgw_auth_s3.cc`, line 1032** (`get_v4_signature`):\n```cpp\nldpp_dout(dpp, 10) << \"generated signature = \" << signature << dendl;\n```\n\n**`src/rgw/rgw_rest_s3.cc`, lines 6321\u20136326** (`LocalEngine::authenticate`):\n```cpp\nldpp_dout(dpp, 15) << \"string_to_sign=\"\n                 << rgw::crypt_sanitize::log_content{string_to_sign}\n                 << dendl;\nldpp_dout(dpp, 15) << \"server signature=\" << server_signature << dendl;\nldpp_dout(dpp, 15) << \"client signature=\" << signature << dendl;\nldpp_dout(dpp, 15) << \"compare=\" << compare << dendl;\n```\n\nNote: The `rgw::crypt_sanitize::log_content` wrapper (used for `string_to_sign`) does provide some protection by redacting content when the `rgw_crypt_require_ssl` option is set, but the signing keys themselves are logged without any sanitization.\n\n#### Impact\n\n- If debug logging (level \u2265 10) is enabled in production \u2014 a common troubleshooting practice \u2014 all intermediate signing keys and computed signatures are written to log files.\n- An attacker with read access to RGW log files (e.g., via a compromised monitoring system, misconfigured log aggregation, or insider threat) can extract `signing_k` and forge signatures for any request within the same date/region/service scope.\n- The `signing_k` is valid for the entire calendar day, giving an attacker up to 24 hours of forged-signature capability per leaked key.\n\n#### Remediation\n\n1. **Remove or gate the signing key log statements** behind a higher debug level (e.g., level 20) or remove them entirely:\n   ```cpp\n   // Either remove these lines, or raise to level 20 and add a clear warning:\n   if (cct->_conf->subsys.should_gather(ceph_subsys_rgw, 20)) [[unlikely]] {\n       ldpp_dout(dpp, 20) << \"WARNING: signing key material in log (dev only)\" << dendl;\n       ldpp_dout(dpp, 20) << \"signing_k = \" << signing_key << dendl;\n   }\n   ```\n\n2. **Apply `rgw::crypt_sanitize` wrappers** to all sensitive key material in log statements, consistent with how `string_to_sign` is already handled in some places.\n\n3. **Audit all log statements** in `rgw_auth_s3.cc` and `rgw_rest_s3.cc` for other instances of sensitive material being logged without sanitization.\n\n4. **Document** that debug log level \u2265 10 should never be enabled in production environments handling sensitive workloads.\n\n---\n\n### Finding 5: No Request Replay Prevention (Nonce Tracking)\n\n**Severity:** MEDIUM  \n**CWE:** CWE-294 \u2014 Authentication Bypass by Capture-replay\n\n#### Description\n\nBeyond the timestamp window (Finding 3), there is no mechanism to detect or prevent replay of the **same signed request** multiple times within the valid window. AWS Signature V4 does not include a nonce by design, but implementations can add server-side replay detection. The RGW implementation does not track previously seen `(access_key_id, date, signature)` tuples, so a captured request can be replayed an unlimited number of times within the 15-minute window.\n\n#### Affected Locations\n\n**`src/rgw/rgw_auth_s3.cc`, lines 265\u2013278** \u2014 `is_time_skew_ok()` only checks the timestamp, not uniqueness:\n```cpp\nbool is_time_skew_ok(time_t t)\n{\n    auto req_tp = ceph::coarse_real_clock::from_time_t(t);\n    auto cur_tp = ceph::coarse_real_clock::now();\n\n    if (std::chrono::abs(cur_tp - req_tp) > RGW_AUTH_GRACE) {\n        return false;\n    }\n    return true;  // \u2190 No nonce check; same request can be replayed\n}\n```\n\n**`src/rgw/rgw_rest_s3.cc`, lines 6265\u20136335** \u2014 `LocalEngine::authenticate()` performs no replay detection:\n```cpp\n// After signature verification succeeds:\nreturn result_t::grant(std::move(apl), completer_factory(k.key));\n// \u2190 No recording of this (access_key, signature) pair to prevent replay\n```\n\n#### Impact\n\n- A captured DELETE request can be replayed to delete an object multiple times (idempotent for the first replay, but relevant for versioned buckets).\n- A captured PUT request can be replayed to overwrite an object with stale data.\n- A captured administrative request (e.g., bucket policy change) can be replayed to re-apply a previously revoked policy.\n- This is particularly dangerous in environments where signed requests are transmitted over partially-trusted networks.\n\n#### Remediation\n\n1. **Implement a bounded nonce cache** using a time-bucketed set of `(access_key_id, signature)` pairs. Entries expire after `RGW_AUTH_GRACE` minutes:\n   ```cpp\n   // Pseudocode for nonce tracking:\n   if (nonce_cache.contains(access_key_id, signature)) {\n       return result_t::reject(-ERR_REQUEST_TIME_SKEWED); // replay detected\n   }\n   nonce_cache.insert(access_key_id, signature, expiry=now+RGW_AUTH_GRACE);\n   ```\n\n2. **Use a distributed cache** (e.g., backed by RADOS) if RGW runs in a multi-instance configuration, to ensure replay detection works across all gateway instances.\n\n3. **Document the replay risk** in the RGW security hardening guide and recommend that operators use HTTPS to reduce the window for request capture.\n\n---\n\n### Finding 6: STS Session Token Encryption Uses AES with a Potentially Weak Key\n\n**Severity:** MEDIUM  \n**CWE:** CWE-326 \u2014 Inadequate Encryption Strength\n\n#### Description\n\nSTS session tokens are encrypted using AES via the `rgw_sts_key` configuration parameter. The key is read directly from the configuration as a plain string and passed to the crypto handler without any key derivation or strength validation beyond what `validate_secret()` provides. If `rgw_sts_key` is set to a short, low-entropy, or default value, the AES encryption protecting session tokens is weakened.\n\n#### Affected Locations\n\n**`src/rgw/rgw_rest_s3.cc`, lines 6367\u20136403** (`STSEngine::get_session_token`):\n```cpp\nauto* cryptohandler = cct->get_crypto_handler(CEPH_CRYPTO_AES);\nif (! cryptohandler) {\n    return -EINVAL;\n}\nstring secret_s = cct->_conf->rgw_sts_key;          // \u2190 raw config string\nbuffer::ptr secret(secret_s.c_str(), secret_s.length());\nint ret = 0;\nif (ret = cryptohandler->validate_secret(secret); ret < 0) {\n    ldpp_dout(dpp, 0) << \"ERROR: Invalid secret key\" << dendl;\n    return -EINVAL;\n}\n// ...\nret = keyhandler->decrypt(en_input, dec_output, &error);\n```\n\n#### Impact\n\n- If `rgw_sts_key` is left at a default or weak value, session tokens can be decrypted by an attacker who obtains them (e.g., from logs or network capture).\n- Decrypted session tokens expose `secret_access_key` and other credential material stored in the `STS::SessionToken` structure.\n\n#### Remediation\n\n1. **Enforce minimum key length** (\u2265 32 bytes for AES-256) and entropy requirements at startup:\n   ```cpp\n   if (secret_s.length() < 32) {\n       ldpp_dout(dpp, 0) << \"ERROR: rgw_sts_key must be at least 32 bytes\" << dendl;\n       return -EINVAL;\n   }\n   ```\n\n2. **Use a key derivation function** (e.g., HKDF or PBKDF2) to derive the AES key from `rgw_sts_key`, rather than using the raw string directly.\n\n3. **Document** that `rgw_sts_key` must be a cryptographically random value of at least 32 bytes, and provide tooling (e.g., `ceph-authtool` or a helper script) to generate a suitable value.\n\n---\n\n## 3. Summary Risk Assessment\n\n| # | Finding | Severity | Exploitability | Impact |\n|---|---------|----------|----------------|--------|\n| 1 | Non-constant-time signature comparison (timing attack) | **HIGH** | Medium \u2014 requires many requests and timing measurement | Signature forgery, authentication bypass |\n| 2 | AWS SigV2 (HMAC-SHA1) accepted with no disable option | **HIGH** | Low \u2014 requires client to use V2 | Weaker auth, no payload signing, no V4-only policy |\n| 3 | 15-minute replay window, no max expiry for V2 presigned URLs | **MEDIUM** | Medium \u2014 requires request capture | Request replay, permanent presigned URLs |\n| 4 | Intermediate signing keys logged at debug level | **MEDIUM** | Low \u2014 requires log access | Signing key exposure, signature forgery |\n| 5 | No nonce/replay tracking within the timestamp window | **MEDIUM** | Medium \u2014 requires request capture | Repeated replay of destructive operations |\n| 6 | STS session token AES key may be weak | **MEDIUM** | Low \u2014 requires token capture + weak key | Session token decryption, credential exposure |\n\n### Overall Risk: **HIGH**\n\nThe combination of a timing-attack-vulnerable signature comparison (Finding 1) and unconditional acceptance of the cryptographically weaker SigV2 (Finding 2) represents a significant authentication security risk. Finding 1 is the most immediately actionable: replacing `std::string::compare()` with `CRYPTO_memcmp()` is a one-line fix per comparison site with no functional impact. Finding 2 requires a configuration option addition and operator communication but is critical for environments that need to enforce modern cryptographic standards.\n\n### Recommended Remediation Priority\n\n1. **(Immediate)** Replace all signature comparisons with `CRYPTO_memcmp()` \u2014 `src/rgw/rgw_rest_s3.cc:6319`, `6454`; `src/rgw/rgw_auth_s3.cc:1228`, `1231`, `1714`.\n2. **(Short-term)** Add `rgw_s3_auth_disable_v2` configuration option and enforce V2 presigned URL expiry cap.\n3. **(Short-term)** Make `RGW_AUTH_GRACE` configurable and reduce the default to 5 minutes.\n4. **(Medium-term)** Remove or gate signing key log statements; apply `crypt_sanitize` wrappers.\n5. **(Medium-term)** Implement nonce tracking for replay prevention.\n6. **(Medium-term)** Enforce minimum entropy requirements for `rgw_sts_key`.\n",

Key files: `rgw_auth_s3.cc`, `rgw_auth_s3.h`, `rgw_rest_s3.cc`.\n\n### Six Findings Documented\n\n| # | Finding | Severity |\n|---|---------|----------|\n| 1 | **Non-constant-time signature comparison** \u2014 `signature.compare(server_signature)` in `LocalEngine::authenticate()` (rgw_rest_s3.cc:6319) and `STSEngine::authenticate()` (rgw_rest_s3.cc:6454), plus `==` comparisons in chunk verification (rgw_auth_s3.cc:1228, 1231, 1714). Vulnerable to timing side-channel attacks. | **HIGH** |\n| 2 | **AWS SigV2 (HMAC-SHA1) accepted with no disable option** \u2014 `AWSGeneralAbstractor::get_auth_data()` (rgw_rest_s3.cc:5567) unconditionally routes to `get_auth_data_v2()` which uses `get_v2_signature()` (HMAC-SHA1). No `rgw_s3_auth_disable_v2` config option exists. | **HIGH** |\n| 3 | **15-minute replay window hardcoded, V2 presigned URLs have no expiry cap** \u2014 `RGW_AUTH_GRACE = std::chrono::minutes{15}` (rgw_auth_s3.h:30) is not configurable; V2 query-string auth (rgw_rest_s3.cc:6011) has no upper bound on the `Expires` parameter. | **MEDIUM** |\n| 4 | **Intermediate signing keys logged at debug level 10** \u2014 `get_v4_signing_key()` (rgw_auth_s3.cc:996-999) logs `date_k`, `region_k`, `service_k`, and `signing_k` without sanitization. | **MEDIUM** |\n| 5 | **No nonce/replay tracking within the timestamp window** \u2014 `is_time_skew_ok()` only validates the timestamp; the same signed request can be replayed unlimited times within the 15-minute window. | **MEDIUM** |\n| 6 | **STS session token AES key may be weak** \u2014 `rgw_sts_key` is used raw without key derivation or minimum entropy enforcement (rgw_rest_s3.cc:6371). | **MEDIUM** |\n\n### Top Remediation Actions\n1. Replace `signature.compare()` / `==` with `CRYPTO_memcmp()` at all 4 comparison sites\n2. Add `rgw_s3_auth_disable_v2` config option to block SigV2\n3. Make `RGW_AUTH_GRACE` configurable (default 5 min) and cap V2 presigned URL expiry at 7 days\n4. Remove or gate signing key log statements behind level \u2265 20 with sanitization"
